      <p>
       <b>
        Quito
       </b>
       (
       <small>
        Spanish pronunciation:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [ˈkito]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_language" title="Quechua language">
        Quechua
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="qu">
         Kitu
        </span>
       </i>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">
        Aymara
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="ay">
         Kitu
        </span>
       </i>
       ), formally
       <b>
        San Francisco de Quito
       </b>
       , is the
       <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">
        capital city
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">
        Ecuador
       </a>
       , and at an elevation of 2,850 metres (9,350 ft) above sea level, it is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_capital_cities_by_altitude" title="List of capital cities by altitude">
        highest official capital city
       </a>
       in the world after
       <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">
        La Paz
       </a>
       , and the one which is closest to the
       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">
        equator
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Contact_Us_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Contact_Us-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is located in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guayllabamba_(river)" title="Guayllabamba (river)">
        Guayllabamba
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_basin" title="River basin">
        river basin
       </a>
       , on the eastern slopes of
       <a href="/wiki/Pichincha_Volcano" title="Pichincha Volcano">
        Pichincha
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eppetroecuador.ec_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-eppetroecuador.ec-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       an active
       <a href="/wiki/Stratovolcano" title="Stratovolcano">
        stratovolcano
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">
        Andes
       </a>
       mountains. With a population of 2,671,191 according to the last census (2014), Quito is the second most populous city in Ecuador, after
       <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">
        Guayaquil
       </a>
       . It is also the capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pichincha_Province" title="Pichincha Province">
        Pichincha province
       </a>
       and the seat of the
       <a href="/wiki/Quito_Canton" title="Quito Canton">
        Metropolitan District of Quito
       </a>
       . The canton recorded a population of 2,239,191 residents in the 2010 national census. In 2008, the city was designated as the headquarters of the
       <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">
        Union of South American Nations
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The historic center of Quito has one of the largest, least-altered and best-preserved historic centers in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">
        the Americas
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-unesco-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Quito and
       <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">
        Kraków
       </a>
       , Poland, were the first
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage" title="World Heritage">
        World Cultural Heritage Sites
       </a>
       declared by
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       , in 1978.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-unesco-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The central square of Quito is located about 25 kilometres (16 mi) south of the
       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">
        equator
       </a>
       ; the city itself extends to within about 1 kilometre (0.62 mi) of zero latitude. A monument and museum marking the general location of the equator is known locally as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Mitad_del_Mundo" title="Ciudad Mitad del Mundo">
         la mitad del mundo
        </a>
       </i>
       (the middle of the world), to avoid confusion, as the word
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         ecuador
        </span>
       </i>
       is
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       for equator.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40">
         <a href="#Sports">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           10
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           Sports
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41">
         <a href="#Crime">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           11
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           Crime
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42">
         <a href="#Notable_people_born_in_Quito">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           12
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           Notable people born in Quito
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43">
         <a href="#Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           13
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           Twin towns and sister cities
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44">
         <a href="#See_also">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           14
          </span>

          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45">

          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Quito" title="Timeline of Quito">
        Timeline of Quito
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_period">
        Pre-Columbian period
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian period">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit">
            improve this section
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            removed
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (July 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The oldest traces of human presence in Quito were excavated by the American archaeologist Robert E. Bell in 1960 on the slopes of the Ilaló volcano, located between the eastern valleys of Los Chillos and Tumbaco. Gatherers and hunters left tools made of obsidian glass dated back 8.000 years BC. The archaeological site herein designated by the name of EI Inga was brought to the attention of Robert E. Bell by Mr. A. Allen Graffham of Ardmore, Oklahoma. While employed as a geologist in Ecuador, Mr. Graffham followed his archaeological interest as an amateur, and he made surface collections at the site during the early months of 1956.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-samnoblemuseum.ou.edu_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-samnoblemuseum.ou.edu-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The discovery of projectile points, particularly specimens exhibiting basal fluting, stimulated his interest, and several visits were made to the site for collecting surface materials. Graffham’s previous interest in PaleoIndian remains and his experience with early man materials found in Kansas and Nebraska in the Central Plains led him to believe that the site was an important discovery.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-samnoblemuseum.ou.edu_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-samnoblemuseum.ou.edu-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The second important vestige of human presence was found in the current neighborhood of Cotocollao (1.500 BC), located in the NW of Quito. The prehistoric village covered over 26 hectares in an area irrigated by many creeks. Near the rectangular there are also burials with pottery and stone offerings. The Cotocollao people extracted and exported obsidian to the coastal region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period">
        Colonial period
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Colonial period">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Virgen_Gu%C3%A1pulo.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="800" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Virgen_Gu%C3%A1pulo.jpg/220px-Virgen_Gu%C3%A1pulo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Virgen_Gu%C3%A1pulo.jpg/330px-Virgen_Gu%C3%A1pulo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Virgen_Gu%C3%A1pulo.jpg/440px-Virgen_Gu%C3%A1pulo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Virgen_Gu%C3%A1pulo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Artwork that shows the city in the mid-18th century.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Urban_evolution_of_colonial_Quito" title="Urban evolution of colonial Quito">
        Urban evolution of colonial Quito
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Indigenous resistance to the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        Spanish invasion
       </a>
       continued during 1534, with the
       <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">
        conquistador
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Almagro" title="Diego de Almagro">
        Diego de Almagro
       </a>
       founding Santiago de Quito (in present-day Colta, near
       <a href="/wiki/Riobamba" title="Riobamba">
        Riobamba
       </a>
       ) on August 15, 1534, later to be renamed San Francisco de Quito on August 28, 1534. The city was later moved to its present location and was refounded on 6 December 1534 by 204 settlers led by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_de_Benalc%C3%A1zar" title="Sebastián de Benalcázar">
        Sebastián de Benalcázar
       </a>
       , who captured
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rumi%C3%B1ahui_(Inca_warrior)" title="Rumiñahui (Inca warrior)">
        Rumiñahui
       </a>
       and effectively ended any organized resistance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rumiñahui was then executed on January 10, 1535.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mapaquito1786.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1693" data-file-width="1900" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Mapaquito1786.jpg/220px-Mapaquito1786.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Mapaquito1786.jpg/330px-Mapaquito1786.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Mapaquito1786.jpg/440px-Mapaquito1786.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mapaquito1786.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map dated 1786, showing the city of Quito in the late 18th century. North is to the right.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On March 28, 1541, Quito was declared a city and on February 23, 1556, was given the title
       <i>
        Muy Noble y Muy Leal Ciudad de San Francisco de Quito
       </i>
       ("Very Noble and Loyal City of San Francisco of Quito"), starting at this point its
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_Evolution_of_Colonial_Quito" title="Urban Evolution of Colonial Quito">
        urban evolution
       </a>
       . In 1563, Quito became the seat of a
       <i>
        Real Audiencia
       </i>
       (administrative district) of Spain and became part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">
        Viceroyalty of Peru
       </a>
       , until 1717 after the
       <i>
        Audiencia
       </i>
       was part of a newly created
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Nueva_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of Nueva Granada">
        Viceroyalty of Nueva Granada
       </a>
       . Its administration on both Viceroyalties remained to Quito. (see
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia_de_Quito" title="Real Audiencia de Quito">
        Real Audiencia de Quito
       </a>
       )
      </p>
      <p>
       As with other places colonized by the Spanish, the colonizers promptly established
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">
        Roman Catholicism
       </a>
       in Quito. The first church (El Belén) was in fact built even before the city had been officially founded. In January 1535, the San Francisco Convent was constructed, the first of about 20 churches and convents built during the colonial period. The Spanish converted the indigenous population to Christianity and used them as labor for construction.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1743, after nearly 300 years of Spanish colonization, Quito was a city of about 10,000 inhabitants.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       On August 10, 1809, an independence movement from Spanish domination started in Quito. On that date, a plan for government was established that placed Juan Pío Montúfar as president with various other prominent figures in other positions of government. However, this initial movement was ultimately defeated on August 2, 1810, when colonial troops came from
       <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">
        Lima
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">
        Peru
       </a>
       , killing the leaders of the uprising along with about 200 settlers.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       A chain of conflicts concluded on May 24, 1822, when
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">
        Antonio José de Sucre
       </a>
       , under the command of
       <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">
        Simón Bolívar
       </a>
       , led troops into the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pichincha" title="Battle of Pichincha">
        Battle of Pichincha
       </a>
       . Their victory marked the independence of Quito and the surrounding areas.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Republican_Ecuador">
        Republican Ecuador
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Republican Ecuador">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 1833, members of the Society of Free Inhabitants of Quito were assassinated by the government after they conspired against it, and on March 6, 1845, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marcist_Revolution" title="Marcist Revolution">
        Marcist Revolution
       </a>
       began. Later, in 1875, the country's president,
       <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Garc%C3%ADa_Moreno" title="Gabriel García Moreno">
        Gabriel García Moreno
       </a>
       , was assassinated in Quito. Two years later, in 1877, Archbishop
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Ignacio_Checa_y_Barba&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="José Ignacio Checa y Barba (page does not exist)">
        José Ignacio Checa y Barba
       </a>
       was killed by poisoning while he was celebrating Mass.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1882, insurgents arose against the regime of dictator
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ignacio_de_Veintimilla" title="Ignacio de Veintimilla">
        Ignacio de Veintimilla
       </a>
       . However, this did not end the violence that was occurring throughout the country. On July 9, 1883, the liberal commander
       <a href="/wiki/Eloy_Alfaro" title="Eloy Alfaro">
        Eloy Alfaro
       </a>
       participated in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guayaquil" title="Battle of Guayaquil">
        Battle of Guayaquil
       </a>
       , and later, after more conflict, became the president of Ecuador on September 4, 1895. Upon completing his second term in 1911, he moved to
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       . When he returned to Ecuador in 1912 and attempted a return to power, he was arrested on January 28, 1912; thrown in prison; and assassinated by a
       <a href="/wiki/Gang" title="Gang">
        mob
       </a>
       that had stormed the prison. His body was dragged through the streets of Quito to a city park, where it was burned.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1932, the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Four_Days%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Four Days' War (page does not exist)">
        Four Days' War
       </a>
       broke out. This was a civil war that followed the election of
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Neptal%C3%AD_Bonifaz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Neptalí Bonifaz (page does not exist)">
        Neptalí Bonifaz
       </a>
       and the subsequent realization that he carried a Peruvian passport. On February 12, 1949, a realistic broadcast of
       <a href="/wiki/H._G._Wells" title="H. G. Wells">
        H. G. Wells
       </a>
       ' novel
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_War_of_the_Worlds_(novel)" title="The War of the Worlds (novel)">
         The War of the Worlds
        </a>
       </i>
       led to citywide panic and the deaths of more than twenty people who died in fires set by mobs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">
        21st century
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 21st century">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 2011, the city's population was 2,239,191 people. Since 2002, the city has begun renewing its historical center and also demolished the old airport and built a new
       <a href="/wiki/Mariscal_Sucre_International_Airport" title="Mariscal Sucre International Airport">
        Mariscal Sucre International Airport
       </a>
       located 45 minutes from central Quito.
      </p>
      <p>
       Between 2003 and 2004, the ecologically friendly bus lines of the Metrobus (Ecovia) were constructed, traversing the city from the north to the south.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Many avenues and roads were extended and enlarged, depressed passages were constructed, and roads were restructured geometrically to increase the flow of traffic. A new subway system is currently under construction.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quito,_Ecuador_Astronaut_Image.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="640" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Quito%2C_Ecuador_Astronaut_Image.jpg/220px-Quito%2C_Ecuador_Astronaut_Image.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Quito%2C_Ecuador_Astronaut_Image.jpg/330px-Quito%2C_Ecuador_Astronaut_Image.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Quito%2C_Ecuador_Astronaut_Image.jpg/440px-Quito%2C_Ecuador_Astronaut_Image.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quito,_Ecuador_Astronaut_Image.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of Quito from the
         <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">
          International Space Station
         </a>
         (north is at the left of the image). Quito sits on the eastern slopes of the
         <a href="/wiki/Pichincha_Volcano" title="Pichincha Volcano">
          Pichincha Volcano
         </a>
         , whose crater is visible.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quito is located in the northern
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highland_(geography)" title="Highland (geography)">
        highlands
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">
        Ecuador
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Guayllabamba_River" title="Guayllabamba River">
        Guayllabamba
       </a>
       river basin. The city is built on a long plateau lying on the east flanks of the Pichincha volcano. The valley of Guayllabamba River where Quito lies is flanked by volcanoes, some of them snow-capped, and visible from the city on a clear day. Quito is the closest
       <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">
        capital city
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">
        equator
       </a>
       . Quito's altitude is listed at 2,820 metres (9,250 feet).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nearby_volcanoes">
        Nearby volcanoes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Nearby volcanoes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Quito's closest volcano is
       <a href="/wiki/Pichincha_Volcano" title="Pichincha Volcano">
        Pichincha
       </a>
       , looming over the western side of the city. Quito is also the only capital in the world to be directly menaced by an active volcano.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Pichincha volcano has several summits, among them Ruku Pichincha at 4,700 metres (15,400 feet)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">
        above sea level
       </a>
       and Wawa Pichincha at 4,794 metres (15,728 feet). Wawa Pichincha is active and being monitored by volcanologists at the geophysical institute of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Escuela_Polit%C3%A9cnica_Nacional" title="Escuela Politécnica Nacional">
        national polytechnic university
       </a>
       . The largest eruption occurred in 1660 when more than 25 centimetres (9.8 inches) of ash covered the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nesdis_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nesdis-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There were three minor eruptions in the 19th century. The latest eruption was recorded on October 5, 1999, when a few puffs of smoke and a large amount of ash were deposited on the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Activity in other nearby volcanoes also can affect the city. In November 2002, after an eruption in the volcano
       <a href="/wiki/Reventador" title="Reventador">
        Reventador
       </a>
       , the city was showered with a layer of fine ash particles to a depth of several centimeters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The volcanoes on the Central Cordillera (Royal Cordillera), east of Quito, surrounding the Guayllabamba valley include
       <a href="/wiki/Cotopaxi" title="Cotopaxi">
        Cotopaxi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sincholagua_Volcano" title="Sincholagua Volcano">
        Sincholagua
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Antisana" title="Antisana">
        Antisana
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cayambe_(volcano)" title="Cayambe (volcano)">
        Cayambe
       </a>
       . Some of the volcanoes of the Western Cordillera, to the west of the Guayllabamba valley, as well as are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pichincha_(volcano)" title="Pichincha (volcano)">
        Pichincha
       </a>
       include
       <a href="/wiki/Illiniza" title="Illiniza">
        Illiniza
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Atacazo" title="Atacazo">
        Atacazo
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pululahua" title="Pululahua">
        Pululahua
       </a>
       (which has the
       <a href="/wiki/Pululahua_Geobotanical_Reserve" title="Pululahua Geobotanical Reserve">
        Pululahua Geobotanical Reserve
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Under the
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen climate classification
       </a>
       , Quito has a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical_highland_climate" title="Subtropical highland climate">
        subtropical highland climate
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peel_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Peel-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (Cfb).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Climate-Data.org_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Climate-Data.org-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because of its elevation and proximity to the equator, Quito has a fairly constant cool climate. The average afternoon high temperature is 21.4 °C (70.5 °F) with an average night-time low of 9.8 °C (49.6 °F).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The annual average temperature is 15.6 °C (60.1 °F).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city has only two seasons: dry and wet. The dry season, June through September (4 months), is referred to as summer; the
       <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">
        wet season
       </a>
       , October through May (8 months), is referred to as winter. Annual precipitation, depending on location, is about 1,000 mm (39 in).
      </p>
      <p>
       Because of its elevation, Quito receives some of the greatest solar radiation in the world, sometimes reaching a
       <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet_index" title="Ultraviolet index">
        UV Index
       </a>
       of 24 by solar noon.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The fact that Quito lies almost on the equator means that high pressure systems are extremely rare. Pressure is stable, so very low pressure systems are also rare. From July 1, 2010 to June 30, 2011, the lowest pressure recorded was 998.2 hPa (29.48 inHg), and the highest was 1,015.2 hPa (29.98 inHg). Despite the absence of high pressure, Quito can still experience settled weather. Generally, the highest pressure is around midnight and the lowest in the mid-afternoon.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Topographical_zones">
        Topographical zones
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Topographical zones">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo,_Ecuador,_2015-07-22,_DD_41.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5187" data-file-width="8688" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_41.JPG/220px-Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_41.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_41.JPG/330px-Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_41.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_41.JPG/440px-Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_41.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo,_Ecuador,_2015-07-22,_DD_41.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Shantytowns up the hills around Quito.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Calle_de_la_Ronda,_Quito,_Ecuador,_2015-07-22,_DD_215.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4267" data-file-width="6156" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Calle_de_la_Ronda%2C_Quito%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_215.JPG/220px-Calle_de_la_Ronda%2C_Quito%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_215.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Calle_de_la_Ronda%2C_Quito%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_215.JPG/330px-Calle_de_la_Ronda%2C_Quito%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_215.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Calle_de_la_Ronda%2C_Quito%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_215.JPG/440px-Calle_de_la_Ronda%2C_Quito%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_215.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Calle_de_la_Ronda,_Quito,_Ecuador,_2015-07-22,_DD_215.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         La Ronda street, one of the most popular areas to go out.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quito is divided into three areas, separated by hills:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        Central: houses the
        <a href="/wiki/Quito#Old_Town" title="Quito">
         colonial old city
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Southern: is mainly industrial and residential, and a working-class housing area.
       </li>
       <li>
        Northern: is the modern Quito, with high-rise buildings, shopping centers, the financial district, and upper-class residential areas and some working-class housing areas.
       </li>
      </ol>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:12_de_Octubre_Avenue_Skyline,_modern_downtown_Quito.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="960" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/12_de_Octubre_Avenue_Skyline%2C_modern_downtown_Quito.png/220px-12_de_Octubre_Avenue_Skyline%2C_modern_downtown_Quito.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/12_de_Octubre_Avenue_Skyline%2C_modern_downtown_Quito.png/330px-12_de_Octubre_Avenue_Skyline%2C_modern_downtown_Quito.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/12_de_Octubre_Avenue_Skyline%2C_modern_downtown_Quito.png/440px-12_de_Octubre_Avenue_Skyline%2C_modern_downtown_Quito.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:12_de_Octubre_Avenue_Skyline,_modern_downtown_Quito.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         12 de Octubre Avenue business area Skyline
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SHYRISBUSINESS.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2736" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/SHYRISBUSINESS.JPG/170px-SHYRISBUSINESS.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/SHYRISBUSINESS.JPG/255px-SHYRISBUSINESS.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/SHYRISBUSINESS.JPG/340px-SHYRISBUSINESS.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SHYRISBUSINESS.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Modern buildings in Quito's growing Financial District
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quito is the largest city in contribution to national GDP, and the second highest in per capita income after
       <a href="/wiki/Cuenca,_Ecuador" title="Cuenca, Ecuador">
        Cuenca
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Quito has the highest level of tax collection in Ecuador, exceeding the national 57% per year 2009, currently being the most important economic region of the country
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       , as the latest "study" conducted by the Central Bank of Ecuador.
      </p>
      <p>
       The top major industries in Quito includes textiles, metals and agriculture, with major crops for export being coffee, sugar, cacao, rice, bananas and palm oil.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/TAME" title="TAME">
         TAME
        </a>
       </b>
       , an airline of Ecuador, has its headquarters in Quito.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Contact_Us_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Contact_Us-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Petroecuador" title="Petroecuador">
         Petroecuador
        </a>
       </b>
       , the largest company in the country and one of the largest in Latin America is headquartered in Quito.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eppetroecuador.ec_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-eppetroecuador.ec-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Headquarters and regional offices of many national and international financial institutions, oil corporations and international businesses are also located in Quito, making it a world class business city.
      </p>
      <p>
       In "The World according to
       <b>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GaWC" title="GaWC">
         GaWC
        </a>
       </b>
       global cities report which measures a city's integration into the world city network, Quito is ranked as a Beta city, as an important world class metropolis which is instrumental in linking its region or state into the world economy.
       <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.lboro.ac.uk/gawc/gawcworlds.html" rel="nofollow">
        [2]
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
        Politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">
        Governance
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Governance">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Quito" title="Mayor of Quito">
        Mayor of Quito
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mauricio_Rodas_Espinel.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2278" data-file-width="1629" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Mauricio_Rodas_Espinel.jpeg/170px-Mauricio_Rodas_Espinel.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Mauricio_Rodas_Espinel.jpeg/255px-Mauricio_Rodas_Espinel.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Mauricio_Rodas_Espinel.jpeg/340px-Mauricio_Rodas_Espinel.jpeg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mauricio_Rodas_Espinel.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Rodas" title="Mauricio Rodas">
          Mauricio Rodas
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Quito" title="Mayor of Quito">
          Mayor of Quito
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quito is governed by a mayor and a 15-member city council. The mayor is elected to a five-year term and can be re-elected. The position also doubles as Mayor of the
       <a href="/wiki/Quito_Canton" title="Quito Canton">
        Metropolitan District of Quito
       </a>
       (the canton). The current mayor is Mauricio Rodas.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_parishes">
        Urban parishes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Urban parishes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In Ecuador, cantons are subdivided into
       <i>
        parishes
       </i>
       , so called because they were originally used by the Catholic Church, but with the secularization and liberalization of the Ecuadorian state, the political parishes were spun off the ones used by the church. Parishes are called
       <i>
        urban
       </i>
       if they are within the boundaries of the seat (capital) of their corresponding canton, and
       <i>
        rural
       </i>
       if outside those boundaries. Inside Quito (the city proper), subdivision into urban parishes depends on the organizations that use these parishes (e.g., the municipality, the electoral tribunals, the postal service, the Ecuadorian statistics institute). The urban parishes of different types are not necessarily coterminous nor the same in number or name.
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2008
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , the municipality of Quito divided the city into 32 urban parishes. These parishes, which are used by the municipality for administrative purposes, are also known as
       <i>
        cabildos
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       since 2001. Since the times of the Metropolitan District of Quito, parishes of this type are also grouped into larger divisions known as
       <i>
        municipal zones
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        zonas municipales
       </i>
       ). These parishes are as follows:
      </p>
      <div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 15em; -webkit-column-width: 15em; column-width: 15em;">
       <ol>
        <li>
         Belisario Quevedo
        </li>
        <li>
         Carcelén
        </li>
        <li>
         Centro Histórico
        </li>
        <li>
         Chilibulo
        </li>
        <li>
         Chillogallo
        </li>
        <li>
         Chimbacalle
        </li>
        <li>
         Cochapamba
        </li>
        <li>
         Comité del Pueblo
        </li>
        <li>
         Concepción
        </li>
        <li>
         Cotocollao
        </li>
        <li>
         El Condado
        </li>
        <li>
         El Inca
        </li>
        <li>
         Guamaní
        </li>
        <li>
         Iñaquito
        </li>
        <li>
         Itchimbía
        </li>
        <li>
         Jipijapa
        </li>
        <li>
         Kennedy
        </li>
        <li>
         La Argelia
        </li>
        <li>
         La Ecuatoriana
        </li>
        <li>
         La Ferroviaria
        </li>
        <li>
         La Libertad
        </li>
        <li>
         La Mena
        </li>
        <li>
         Magdalena
        </li>
        <li>
         Mariscal Sucre
        </li>
        <li>
         Ponceano
        </li>
        <li>
         Puengasí
        </li>
        <li>
         Quitumbe
        </li>
        <li>
         Rumipamba
        </li>
        <li>
         San Bartolo
        </li>
        <li>
         San Juan
        </li>
        <li>
         Solanda
        </li>
        <li>
         Turubamba
        </li>
       </ol>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecclesiastical_parishes">
        Ecclesiastical parishes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ecclesiastical parishes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Quito" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Quito">
        Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Quito
       </a>
       divides the city into 167 parishes, which are grouped into 17 zones.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">
        Public transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Public transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bici_Q.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Bici_Q.jpg/220px-Bici_Q.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Bici_Q.jpg/330px-Bici_Q.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Bici_Q.jpg/440px-Bici_Q.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bici_Q.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Bici Q station in northern Quito. Bici Q is the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicycle_sharing_system" title="Bicycle sharing system">
          Bicycle sharing system
         </a>
         started by the municipal government of the city
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/MetrobusQ" title="MetrobusQ">
        MetrobusQ
       </a>
       network, also known as "Red Integrada de Transporte Público", is the
       <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">
        bus rapid transit
       </a>
       system running in Quito, and it goes through the city from south to north. It's divided into three sections—the green line (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quito_trolleybus_system" title="Quito trolleybus system">
        the central trolleybus
       </a>
       , known as
       <i>
        El Trole
       </i>
       ), the red line (the north-east
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ecov%C3%ADa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ecovía (page does not exist)">
        Ecovía
       </a>
       ), and the blue line (the north-west Corridor Central). In addition to the
       <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">
        bus rapid transit
       </a>
       system, there are many buses running in the city. The buses have both a name and a number, and they have a fixed route. Taxi cabs are all yellow, and they have meters that show the fare. There are nearly 8,800 registered
       <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">
        taxicabs
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In August 2012 the
       <a href="/wiki/Municipality_of_Quito" title="Municipality of Quito">
        Municipality of Quito
       </a>
       government established a municipal
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicycle_sharing_system" title="Bicycle sharing system">
        bicycle sharing system
       </a>
       called Bici Q.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Road_transport">
        Road transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Road transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Although public transportation is the primary form of travel in the city, including fleets of taxis that constantly cruise the roadways, the use of private vehicles has increased substantially during the past decade.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because of growing road congestion in many areas, there were plans to construct a
       <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">
        light rail
       </a>
       system, which were conceived to replace the northern portion of the
       <i>
        Trole
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These plans have been ruled out and replaced by the construction of the
       <a href="/wiki/Quito_Metro" title="Quito Metro">
        first metro line
       </a>
       (subway) in 2012. It is expected to be operational by 2019, joining the existing public transportation network.
      </p>
      <p>
       <b>
        Roads, avenues and streets
       </b>
       Because Quito is about 40 km (25 mi) long and 5 km (3.1 mi) at its widest, most of the important avenues of the city extend from north to south. The two main motorways that go from the northern part of the city to the southern are Avenue Oriental (Corridor Periférico Oriental) on the eastern hills that border the city, and Avenue Occidental on the western side of the city on the Pichincha volcano. The street 10 de Agosto also runs north to south through most of the city, running down the middle of it. The historic centre of the city is based on a grid pattern, despite the hills, with the streets Venezuela, Chile, García Moreno, and Guayaquil being the most important.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transport">
        Air transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Air transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Acceso_NAIQ.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Acceso_NAIQ.JPG/220px-Acceso_NAIQ.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Acceso_NAIQ.JPG/330px-Acceso_NAIQ.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Acceso_NAIQ.JPG/440px-Acceso_NAIQ.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Acceso_NAIQ.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Mariscal_Sucre_International_Airport" title="Mariscal Sucre International Airport">
          Mariscal Sucre International Airport
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Mariscal_Sucre_International_Airport" title="Mariscal Sucre International Airport">
        Mariscal Sucre International Airport
       </a>
       serves as the city's principal airport for passenger travel and freight. The airport is located 18 kilometres (11 mi) east of the city's center in the Tababela parish. It began operations on February 20, 2013, replacing the
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Mariscal_Sucre_International_Airport" title="Old Mariscal Sucre International Airport">
        Old Mariscal Sucre International Airport
       </a>
       located 10 kilometres (6.2 mi) north of the city center within city limits. The old airport was replaced due to tall buildings and nighttime fog that made landing from the south difficult. The old airport has become a metropolitan park.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">
        Rail
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Rail">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       There is a railroad that goes through the southern part of Quito and passes through the
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Estaci%C3%B3n_de_Chimbacalle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Estación de Chimbacalle (page does not exist)">
         Estación de Chimbacalle
        </a>
       </i>
       . It is managed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Empresa_de_Ferrocarriles_Ecuatorianos" title="Empresa de Ferrocarriles Ecuatorianos">
        Empresa de Ferrocarriles Ecuatorianos
       </a>
       (EFE). This form of transport is nowadays used mostly for tourism.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Subway">
        Subway
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Subway">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       A major construction project began in 2012 for a 23 kilometres (14 mi) metro subway system (
       <a href="/wiki/Quito_Metro" title="Quito Metro">
        Quito Metro
       </a>
       ). Phase 1 entails the construction of stations at La Magdalena and El Labrador. Phase 2 will involve 13 more stations, a depot and sub-systems. The project is expected to carry 400,000 passengers per day and to cost USD$1.5 billion with finance coming from the World Bank, the Inter-American Development Bank (IDB), the European Investment Bank (EIB) and the Development Bank of Latin America (CAF)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and is expected to be operational in 2019.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news1_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-news1-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news2_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-news2-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Points_of_interest">
        Points of interest
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Points of interest">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_center">
        Historic center
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Historic center">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quito_Centro_Hist%C3%B3rico.JPG">
         <img alt="Quito Centro Histórico.JPG" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4134" data-file-width="2797" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Quito_Centro_Hist%C3%B3rico.JPG/170px-Quito_Centro_Hist%C3%B3rico.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Quito_Centro_Hist%C3%B3rico.JPG/255px-Quito_Centro_Hist%C3%B3rico.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Quito_Centro_Hist%C3%B3rico.JPG/340px-Quito_Centro_Hist%C3%B3rico.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quito_Centro_Hist%C3%B3rico.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quito has the largest, least-altered, and best-preserved historic center in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">
        the Americas
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco_5-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-unesco-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This center was, together with the historic centre of
       <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">
        Kraków
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">
        Poland
       </a>
       , the first to be declared
       <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
        World Heritage Site
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       on 18 September 1978. The Historic Centre of Quito is located in the center south of the capital on an area of 320 hectares (790 acres), and is considered one of the most important historic areas in Latin America.There are about 130 monumental buildings (which host a variety of pictorial art and sculpture, mostly religion inspired, in a multi-faceted range of schools and styles) and 5,000 properties registered in the municipal inventory of heritage properties.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Carondelet Palace
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Carondelet_Palace" title="Carondelet Palace">
        Carondelet Palace
       </a>
       (Spanish:
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         Palacio de Carondelet
        </span>
       </i>
       ) is the seat of government of the Republic of
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">
        Ecuador
       </a>
       , located in the historical center of Quito. The palace is in the nerve center of the public space known as Independence Square or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plaza_Grande" title="Plaza Grande">
        Plaza Grande
       </a>
       (colonial name), around which were built in addition the Archbishop's Palace, the Municipal Palace, the
       <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Plaza_Grande" title="Hotel Plaza Grande">
        Hotel Plaza Grande
       </a>
       and the Metropolitan Cathedral. During the Republican era, almost all the presidents (constitutional, internees and dictators) have dispatched from this building, which is the seat of Government of the Republic of Ecuador. In addition to the administrative units in the third level of the Palace is the presidential residence, a luxurious colonial-style apartment in which the President and his family dwell.
       <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Correa" title="Rafael Correa">
        Rafael Correa
       </a>
       , president since 2007, converted the presidential compound into a museum accessible to all who wish to visit it.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Basilica del Voto Nacional
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       This monumental
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basilica_del_Voto_Nacional" title="Basilica del Voto Nacional">
        Basilica del Voto Nacional
       </a>
       is the most important neo-Gothic building in Ecuador and one of the most representative of the American continent. It was once the largest in the New World.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Cathedral of Quito
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Quito" title="Cathedral of Quito">
        Cathedral of Quito
       </a>
       , is one of the largest religious symbols of spiritual value for the Catholic community in the city. This church began its construction in 1562, seventeen years after the diocese of Quito was created (1545). The church building was completed in 1806, during the administration of President of the Real Audiencia Baron Héctor de Carondelet.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       One of the events that took place in this cathedral was the murder of the Bishop of Quito, José Ignacio Checa y Barba, who during the mass of
       <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday" title="Good Friday">
        Good Friday
       </a>
       on 30 March 1877 was poisoned with strychnine dissolved in the consecrated wine. The cathedral is also the burial place of the remains of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Marshal" title="Grand Marshal">
        Grand Marshal
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">
        Antonio José de Sucre
       </a>
       and also of several presidents of the Republic, as well as of bishops and priests who died in the diocese. The cathedral is located on the south side of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plaza_de_La_Independencia" title="Plaza de La Independencia">
        Plaza de La Independencia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Church of La Compañía de Jesús
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Society_of_Jesus_(Quito,_Ecuador)" title="Church of the Society of Jesus (Quito, Ecuador)">
        Church of La Compañía
       </a>
       began construction in 1605; it took 160 years to be built. By 1765 the work was completed with the construction of the façade. This was done by Native Americans who carefully shaped the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Baroque_architecture" title="Spanish Baroque architecture">
        Baroque style
       </a>
       in one of the most complete examples of this art in the Americas.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Church of San Francisco
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_and_Convent_of_St._Francis" title="Church and Convent of St. Francis">
        San Francisco
       </a>
       is the largest of the existing architectural ensembles in the historic centers of cities in Latin America. The construction of the church began in 1550, on land adjacent to the plaza where the Native Americans engaged in the barter of products.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Church of El Sagrario
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       In colonial times, the
       <a href="/wiki/La_Iglesia_de_El_Sagrario_(Quito)" title="La Iglesia de El Sagrario (Quito)">
        Church of El Sagrario
       </a>
       was one of the largest architectural marvels of Quito. The construction is of the Italian Renaissance style and it was built in the late 17th century. It has a screen that supports its sculptures and decorations. This structure was built by Bernardo de Legarda. Its central arch leads to a dome decorated with frescoes of biblical scenes featuring archangels. It was done by Francisco Albán. The altarpiece was gilded by Legarda. It is located on Calle García Moreno, near the Cathedral.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Church of Santo Domingo
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit">
            improve this section
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            removed
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (August 2011)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Although they arrived in Quito in 1541, in 1580 the Dominicans started to build their temple, using the plans and direction of Francisco Becerra. The work was completed in the first half of the 17th century. Inside the church are valuable structures, such as the neo-Gothic main altar. This was placed in the late 19th century by Italian Dominicans. The roof of the Mudéjar style church features paintings of martyrs of the Order of Saint Dominic. The roof of the nave is composed of a pair and knuckle frame, coated inside by pieces of tracery. In the museum located on the north side of the lower cloister are wonderful pieces of great Quito sculptors such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Dominic" title="Saint Dominic">
        Saint Dominic de Guzmán
       </a>
       by Father Carlos, the
       <a href="/wiki/John_of_God" title="John of God">
        Saint John of God
       </a>
       by Caspicara, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas" title="Thomas Aquinas">
        Saint Thomas Aquinas
       </a>
       by Legarda. Another Baroque piece that stands is the Chapel of Nuestra Señora del Rosario, which is a recognizable feature of the architecture of Quito. This chapel was built beside the church, in the gospel side. In this was founded the largest fraternity in the city of Quito.
      </p>

           </a>
           , office and house of the Presidents of Ecuador.
          </p>

         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
