       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo,_Ecuador,_2015-07-22,_DD_34-37_PAN.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4349" data-file-width="15877" height="60" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_34-37_PAN.JPG/220px-Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_34-37_PAN.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_34-37_PAN.JPG/330px-Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_34-37_PAN.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_34-37_PAN.JPG/440px-Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_34-37_PAN.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_Quito_desde_El_Panecillo,_Ecuador,_2015-07-22,_DD_34-37_PAN.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of Quito from El Panecillo.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/El_Panecillo" title="El Panecillo">
        El Panecillo
       </a>
       is a hill located in the middle west of the city at an altitude of about 3,016 metres (9,895 ft)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">
        above sea level
       </a>
       . A monument to the Virgin Mary is located on top of El Panecillo and is visible from most of the city of Quito. In 1976, the Spanish artist Agustín de la Herrán Matorras was commissioned by the religious order of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oblate_(religion)" title="Oblate (religion)">
        Oblates
       </a>
       to build a 41 metres (135 ft)–tall aluminum monument of a
       <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(art)" title="Madonna (art)">
        madonna
       </a>
       , which was assembled on a high pedestal on the top of Panecillo. The statue of the Virgin on the Panecillo is a replica of a sculpture made by Bernardo de Legarda in 1732. So this monument is also called Virgen de Legarda or Virgen del Panecillo.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="La_Mariscal">
        La Mariscal
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: La Mariscal">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       This area is considered the city's entertainment center. It is the meeting point of local people and tourists. Its cosmopolitan atmosphere is expressed through the variety of gastronomy, artistic, cultural options and the large number of hotels and inns, travel agencies, language and dance schools, stores, bars, and discothèques that light up when the sun hides.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Plaza_Foch_.28La_Zona.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plaza_Foch_(La_Zona)">
        Plaza Foch (La Zona)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Plaza Foch (La Zona)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Plazafoch.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="638" data-file-width="960" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Plazafoch.jpg/220px-Plazafoch.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Plazafoch.jpg/330px-Plazafoch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Plazafoch.jpg/440px-Plazafoch.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Plazafoch.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Plaza Foch
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       This area is considered the
       <i>
        zona rosa
       </i>
       of the city. It is constituted of various night clubs and bars and has a great night vibe. Plaza Foch is most populated Thursday-Saturday, and gets tourists from all over the world. For this reason, prices for liquor and beer are expensive compared to other places in Quito.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Parks">
        Parks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Parks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb noresize tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:808px;">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="">
        <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parque_el_Arbolito.jpg" title="Arbolito Park">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="1264" data-file-width="6384" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Parque_el_Arbolito.jpg/800px-Parque_el_Arbolito.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Parque_el_Arbolito.jpg/1200px-Parque_el_Arbolito.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Parque_el_Arbolito.jpg/1600px-Parque_el_Arbolito.jpg 2x" width="800"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Parque_el_Arbolito.jpg" title="File:Parque el Arbolito.jpg">
          </a>
         </div>
         Arbolito Park
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitano">
        Metropolitano
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Metropolitano">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Parque Metropolitano Guanguiltagua
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is the largest urban park in
       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">
        South America
       </a>
       at 1,376 acres (5.57 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) (as reference, New York's
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">
        Central Park
       </a>
       is 843 acres (341 ha)). The park is located in northern Quito, on the hill of
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bellavista,_Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bellavista, Quito (page does not exist)">
        Bellavista
       </a>
       behind
       <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Atahualpa" title="Estadio Olímpico Atahualpa">
        Estadio Olímpico Atahualpa
       </a>
       . The park is suited for mountain biking, walking, and running. Most of it is
       <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">
        eucalyptus
       </a>
       forest with trails, but there also are numerous sculptures on display. The park has four sites that can be used for picnics or barbecues, and the eastern section has a view of
       <a href="/wiki/Cotopaxi" title="Cotopaxi">
        Cotopaxi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Antisana" title="Antisana">
        Antisana
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guayllabamba_(river)" title="Guayllabamba (river)">
        Guayllabamba
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_basin" title="River basin">
        river basin
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bicentenario">
        Bicentenario
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Bicentenario">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Parque Bicentenario is the second largest urban park in Quito (surpassed only by the Parque Metropolitano), located in the site of the
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Mariscal_Sucre_International_Airport" title="Old Mariscal Sucre International Airport">
        Old Mariscal Sucre International Airport
       </a>
       . It was inaugurated on April 27, 2013. This park has 200 acres (81 ha), and it's located at 2,800 m (9,186 ft), above mean sea level. The former runway has been converted into recreational space with lanes painted for bicycles and pedestrians. There are play structures and games for children. As well, there is outdoor exercise equipment for adults. The park contains a man-made pond and more than one thousand trees, many newly planted. The park also hosts cultural exhibits and outdoor concerts.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="La_Carolina">
        La Carolina
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: La Carolina">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_Carolina_5.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1037" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/La_Carolina_5.jpg/220px-La_Carolina_5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/La_Carolina_5.jpg/330px-La_Carolina_5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/La_Carolina_5.jpg/440px-La_Carolina_5.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_Carolina_5.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Parque_La_Carolina" title="Parque La Carolina">
          La Carolina park
         </a>
         next to Amazonas Avenue
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Parque_La_Carolina" title="Parque La Carolina">
        La Carolina
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is a 165.5-acre (670,000 m²) park in the centre of the Quito main business area, bordered by the avenues Río Amazonas, de los Shyris, Naciones Unidas, Eloy Alfaro, and de la República. This park started from the expropriation of the farm La Carolina in 1939. The design of the park was made by the Dirección Metropolitana de Planificación Territorial (DMPT).
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">
        Pope John Paul II
       </a>
       headed a great mass in the park during his visit to Ecuador in 1985.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       A giant cross has been built in this place.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="El_Ejido">
        El Ejido
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: El Ejido">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/El_Ejido" title="El Ejido">
        El Ejido
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is the fourth-largest park of Quito (after Metropolitan, Bicentenario and La Carolina), and it divides the old part of the city from the modern one. This park is known for handicrafts available for sale every Saturday and Sunday, with all pricing subject to negotiation (that is, haggling). Local painters sell copies of paintings by
       <a href="/wiki/Oswaldo_Guayasam%C3%ADn" title="Oswaldo Guayasamín">
        Oswaldo Guayasamín
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Kingman" title="Eduardo Kingman">
        Eduardo Kingman
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Endara_Crow" title="Gonzalo Endara Crow">
        Gonzalo Endara Crow
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Otavalo_people" title="Otavalo people">
        Otavaleños
       </a>
       sell traditional sweaters,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ponchos" title="Ponchos">
        ponchos
       </a>
       , carpets, and jewelry.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Gu.C3.A1pulo">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Guápulo">
        Guápulo
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Guápulo">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:(Gu%C3%A1pulo)_Calle_pic._b.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4608" data-file-width="3456" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/%28Gu%C3%A1pulo%29_Calle_pic._b.JPG/170px-%28Gu%C3%A1pulo%29_Calle_pic._b.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/%28Gu%C3%A1pulo%29_Calle_pic._b.JPG/255px-%28Gu%C3%A1pulo%29_Calle_pic._b.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/%28Gu%C3%A1pulo%29_Calle_pic._b.JPG/340px-%28Gu%C3%A1pulo%29_Calle_pic._b.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:(Gu%C3%A1pulo)_Calle_pic._b.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Street in Guápulo.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Set on the side on a cliff with González Suárez Street, one of the most famous in Quito and to the other side the valley and further in the distance, the Amazon Jungle.
       <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A1pulo" title="Guápulo">
        Guápulo
       </a>
       is a district of Quito, Ecuador, also called an electoral parish (
       <i>
        parroquia electoral urbana
       </i>
       ). The parish was established as a result of the October 2004 political elections when the city was divided into 19 urban electoral parishes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Set behind Hotel Quito, the neighborhood of Guápulo runs down the winding Camino de Orellana, from González Suárez to Calle de los Conquistadores, the main road out of Quito and to the neighboring suburbs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Often considered an artsy, bohemian neighborhood of Quito, Guápulo is home to many local artists and a couple of hippy cafés/bars. Every year on September 7 the guapuleños honor their neighborhood with the Fiestas de Guápulo, a fantastic celebration complete with costumes, parade, food, drink, song, dance, and fireworks.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="La_Alameda">
        La Alameda
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: La Alameda">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The long triangular La Alameda is located at the beginning of street Guayaquil, where the historic centre begins. It has an impressive monument of
       <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">
        Simón Bolívar
       </a>
       at the apex. There are several other interesting monuments in this park. In the centre of the park is the Quito Observatory, which was opened by President García Moreno in 1873 and is the oldest observatory in Latin America.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       It is used for both meteorology and astronomy. At the north end of the park are two ornamental lakes, where rowboats can be rented.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="TeleferiQo">
        TeleferiQo
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: TeleferiQo">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Telef%C3%A9riQo" title="TelefériQo">
        TelefériQo
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teleferico_de_quito23.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="239" data-file-width="500" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Teleferico_de_quito23.JPG/220px-Teleferico_de_quito23.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Teleferico_de_quito23.JPG/330px-Teleferico_de_quito23.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Teleferico_de_quito23.JPG/440px-Teleferico_de_quito23.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teleferico_de_quito23.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Telef%C3%A9riQo" title="TelefériQo">
          TelefériQo
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Aerial tramway Station at Cruz Loma (part of the Pichincha mountain complex at about 4,000 metres (13,000 ft)). Since July 2005, Quito has had an
       <a href="/wiki/Aerial_tramway" title="Aerial tramway">
        aerial tramway
       </a>
       , known as the "Telefériqo", from the city centre to the hill known as Cruz Loma on the east side of the Pichincha volcano. The ride takes visitors to an elevation of about 4,100 metres (13,500 ft). There are also trails for hiking and areas where pictures can be taken of Quito. Because of the increased elevation and the wind on the mountain, it is considerably cooler.
      </p>
      <p>
       Besides the aerial tramway to Cruz Loma, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telef%C3%A9riqo" title="Telefériqo">
        Telefériqo
       </a>
       as a whole is a visitor centre that includes an amusement park (
       <a href="/wiki/Vulqano_Park" title="Vulqano Park">
        Vulqano Park
       </a>
       ), fine-dining restaurants, Go Karts, Paint Ball, shopping malls, an extensive food court, and other attractions.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_the_city">
        Outside the city
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Outside the city">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mitad_del_Mundo,_Quito,_Ecuador,_2015-07-22,_DD_06.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7855" data-file-width="5184" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Mitad_del_Mundo%2C_Quito%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_06.JPG/170px-Mitad_del_Mundo%2C_Quito%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_06.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Mitad_del_Mundo%2C_Quito%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_06.JPG/255px-Mitad_del_Mundo%2C_Quito%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Mitad_del_Mundo%2C_Quito%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_06.JPG/340px-Mitad_del_Mundo%2C_Quito%2C_Ecuador%2C_2015-07-22%2C_DD_06.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mitad_del_Mundo,_Quito,_Ecuador,_2015-07-22,_DD_06.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The monument at La Mitad del Mundo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       La
       <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Mitad_del_Mundo" title="Ciudad Mitad del Mundo">
        Mitad del Mundo
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (the middle of the world) is a small village administered by the prefecture of the province of Pichincha, 35 kilometres (22 mi) north of Quito. It has since been determined, with the use of
       <a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">
        Global Positioning System
       </a>
       technology, that the actual equator is some 240 metres (790 ft) north of the monument area. Nearby is the Intiñan Solar Museum, which may be closer to the true equator.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Intiñan Solar Museum provides a demonstration which purports to show the
       <a href="/wiki/Coriolis_force" title="Coriolis force">
        Coriolis force
       </a>
       causing a clockwise rotation of sink water a few meters south of the equator and a counterclockwise rotation a few meters north,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but many scientific sources claim that this is implausible.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (An African equator demonstration purports to show the Coriolis force causing a clockwise rotation of sink water a few meters north of the equator and a counterclockwise rotation a few meters south.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Pululahua_Geobotanical_Reserve" title="Pululahua Geobotanical Reserve">
        Pululahua Geobotanical Reserve
       </a>
       , located a few miles northwest from La Mitad del Mundo, contains the Pululahua volcano, whose
       <a href="/wiki/Caldera" title="Caldera">
        caldera
       </a>
       (crater) is visible from a spot easily accessible by car. It is believed to be one of only a few in the world with human inhabitants.
      </p>
      <p>
       Quito Zoo,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       located near the rural parish of
       <a href="/wiki/Guayllabamba" title="Guayllabamba">
        Guayllabamba
       </a>
       , about 20 kilometres (12 mi) outside Quito, has the biggest collection of native fauna in Ecuador, including several kinds of animals that are sometimes targeted in Ecuador in the illegal fur trade. The Zoo works in conservation and education in Ecuador and has successfully bred the endangered Andean condor.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Maquipucuna" title="Maquipucuna">
        Maquipucuna Reserve
       </a>
       is located in Quito's rural parish of Nanegal. This 14,000 acre high biodiversity rainforest/cloudforest reserve protects over 1966 species of plants
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (10% of Ecuador's plant diversity) and close to 400 bird species. This reserve, which is surrounded by a 34,000 acre protected forest, was declared an IBA (Important Bird Area) in 2005
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and is the core of the conservation corridor for the
       <a href="/wiki/Spectacled_bear" title="Spectacled bear">
        Spectacled bear
       </a>
       (Andean bear)declared in 2013.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The area has an ecolodge located in the northern end of the Reserve where the Spectacled bear can be sighted for about two months every year.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some of the other nearby natural attractions are:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Maquipucuna" title="Maquipucuna">
         Maquipucuna Reserve
        </a>
        Conservation, community projects, bird watching, spectacled bear watching
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Bellavista_Cloud_Forest_Reserve" title="Bellavista Cloud Forest Reserve">
         Bellavista Cloud Forest Reserve
        </a>
        conservation and bird watching lodge
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cayambe_(volcano)" title="Cayambe (volcano)">
         Cayambe
        </a>
        – Coca Ecological Reserve
        <ul>
         <li>
          Papallacta &amp; Oyacachi thermal springs
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cotopaxi" title="Cotopaxi">
         Cotopaxi
        </a>
        National Park
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Mindo,_Ecuador" title="Mindo, Ecuador">
         Mindo
        </a>
        Nambillo cloud forest
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Illiniza" title="Illiniza">
         Illiniza
        </a>
        volcano
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Pasochoa" title="Pasochoa">
         Pasochoa
        </a>
        Wildlife Refuge
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Pichincha_Volcano" title="Pichincha Volcano">
         Pichincha
        </a>
        volcano with its peaks Wawa Pichincha and Ruku Pichincha
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Quito is a city with a mix of modern-day and traditional culture. There is a big presence of Catholics in Quito, most notably,
       <a href="/wiki/Easter_Week" title="Easter Week">
        Easter Week
       </a>
       is a significant celebration in all Latin American countries, but Quito observes this tradition with a series of ceremonies and rituals that begin on
       <a href="/wiki/Palm_Sunday" title="Palm Sunday">
        Palm Sunday
       </a>
       . At noon on
       <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday" title="Good Friday">
        Good Friday
       </a>
       , the March of the Penitents proceeds from the Church of San Francisco, in memory of the hour that Pontius Pilate sentenced Jesus to be crucified.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>

       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Universities_66-0">

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">
        Libraries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Libraries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       One of the oldest and most important library in Ecuador is the Central University Library in Quito. It was founded in 1586 and has 170,000 volumes in its possession.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">
        Museums
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Museums">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         Museo de Arte Contemporaneas
        </b>
        – Located north of Basilica del Voto Nacional, this museum has permanent and temporary exhibitions. The historic building used to be a big military hospital and was renewed for its new purpose.
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alabado_House_Pre-Columbian_Art_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alabado House Pre-Columbian Art Museum (page does not exist)">
          Casa del Alabado
         </a>
        </b>
        – Located just south of Plaza San Francisco, this is the Old Town's newest museum and houses a collection of pre-colonial art. The building is one of the oldest houses in the city.
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/City_Museum_(Quito)" title="City Museum (Quito)">
          Museo de la Ciudad
         </a>
        </b>
        – A museum dedicated to the history of Quito. Located just east of the Plaza de Santo Domingo.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
         <a href="#cite_note-68">
          [68]
         </a>
        </sup>
        It is housed in the buildings of the former
        <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_de_Dios_Hospital_(Quito)" title="San Juan de Dios Hospital (Quito)">
         San Juan de Dios Hospital
        </a>
        , a UNESCO Cultural World Heritage Site.
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/La_Capilla_del_Hombre" title="La Capilla del Hombre">
          La Capilla del Hombre
         </a>
        </b>
        – A museum showcasing the work of legendary Ecuadorian Artist
        <a href="/wiki/Oswaldo_Guayasam%C3%ADn" title="Oswaldo Guayasamín">
         Oswaldo Guayasamín
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Ecuador_National_Museum_of_Medicine" title="Ecuador National Museum of Medicine">
         Ecuador National Museum of Medicine
        </a>
        – A museum dedicated to the history of medicine
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
         <a href="#cite_note-69">
          [69]
         </a>
        </sup>
        in Quito, founded by
        <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Estrella_Aguirre" title="Eduardo Estrella Aguirre">
         Eduardo Estrella Aguirre
        </a>
        . Estrella was in the Archives of the
        <a href="/wiki/Real_Jard%C3%ADn_Bot%C3%A1nico_de_Madrid" title="Real Jardín Botánico de Madrid">
         Royal Botanical Gardens in Madrid, Spain
        </a>
        in 1985 and uncovered the lost papers and paintings documenting one of the first expeditions to South America. In Madrid Spain, Estrella worked for many years and documented his observations in the archive and was able to publish the hard work of Juan Tafalla in a book called
        <a href="/wiki/Flora_Huayaquilensis" title="Flora Huayaquilensis">
         Flora Huayaquilensis
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Museo Casa de Sucre
        </b>
        – This museum is dedicated to life of Mariscal
        <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">
         Antonio José de Sucre
        </a>
        , a hero of Ecuadorian independence. The ground floor has an array of weapons and military relics, many of which belonged to Sucre himself. The second floor has been restored to what it might have looked like in Sucre's time.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
         <a href="#cite_note-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Museo Nacional del Banco Central del Ecuador
        </b>
        – This art museum houses 5 displays. Each one covers a different time period, ranging from prehistory to modern Ecuador.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
         <a href="#cite_note-71">
          [71]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Estadio_de_LDU_Tribuna_E.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Estadio_de_LDU_Tribuna_E.jpg/220px-Estadio_de_LDU_Tribuna_E.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Estadio_de_LDU_Tribuna_E.jpg/330px-Estadio_de_LDU_Tribuna_E.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Estadio_de_LDU_Tribuna_E.jpg/440px-Estadio_de_LDU_Tribuna_E.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Estadio_de_LDU_Tribuna_E.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Estadio Casa Blanca, the newest stadium in Quito and home of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liga_Deportiva_Universitaria_de_Quito" title="Liga Deportiva Universitaria de Quito">
          LDU Quito
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Quito is home to seven prominent football clubs in the country. The city's top clubs (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liga_Deportiva_Universitaria_de_Quito" title="Liga Deportiva Universitaria de Quito">
        LDU Quito
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_El_Nacional" title="Club Deportivo El Nacional">
        El Nacional
       </a>
       ) have won a total of 28 national championships, over half of all championships played.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sociedad_Deportivo_Quito" title="Sociedad Deportivo Quito">
        Deportivo Quito
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sociedad_Deportiva_Aucas" title="Sociedad Deportiva Aucas">
        Aucas
       </a>
       were the first home teams to play in the national league. Deportivo Quito was also the first out of the three home teams to win the title.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liga_Deportiva_Universitaria_de_Quito" title="Liga Deportiva Universitaria de Quito">
        LDU Quito
       </a>
       is the only Ecuadorian club to have won 4 continental titles.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_El_Nacional" title="Club Deportivo El Nacional">
        El Nacional
       </a>
       is the second most titled team in Ecuador's history.
       <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica_de_Quito" title="América de Quito">
        América de Quito
       </a>
       was one of the most titled clubs in the past but has recently played in the lower divisions.
      </p>
      <p>
       The professional teams in the city are:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica_de_Quito" title="América de Quito">
         América de Quito
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sociedad_Deportiva_Aucas" title="Sociedad Deportiva Aucas">
         Aucas
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sociedad_Deportivo_Quito" title="Sociedad Deportivo Quito">
         Deportivo Quito
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_El_Nacional" title="Club Deportivo El Nacional">
         El Nacional
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_ESPOLI" title="Club Deportivo ESPOLI">
         ESPOLI
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liga_Deportiva_Universitaria_de_Quito" title="Liga Deportiva Universitaria de Quito">
         LDU Quito
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_Universidad_Cat%C3%B3lica_del_Ecuador" title="Club Deportivo Universidad Católica del Ecuador">
         Universidad Católica
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       One of the more interesting facts of Quito is that the stadiums are located over 2,800 metres (9,200 feet)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" title="Above sea level">
        above sea level
       </a>
       , this gives the city the special feature and a great advantage for local teams when they play against foreign teams and it is one of the reasons that has allowed Ecuador to qualify for the last two World Cups.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">
        Crime
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Crime">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Ecuador" title="Crime in Ecuador">
        Crime in Ecuador
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_State" title="U.S. Department of State">
        U.S. Department of State
       </a>
       notes that
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petty_theft" title="Petty theft">
        petty theft
       </a>
       is the most common crime issue facing tourists in Quito,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       stating in 2015: "Pickpocketing, purse snatching, robbery, bag slashing, and hotel room theft are the most common types of crimes committed against U.S. citizens."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people_born_in_Quito">
        Notable people born in Quito
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quito&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Notable people born in Quito">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Poet
        <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Carrera_Andrade" title="Jorge Carrera Andrade">
         Jorge Carrera Andrade
        </a>
        (b. 1902, Quito – d. 1978, Quito)
       </li>
       <li>
        Novelist
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jorge_Icaza" title="Jorge Icaza">
         Jorge Icaza
        </a>
        (b. 1906, Quito – d. 1978, Quito)
       </li>
       <li>
        Film Director
        <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_Cordero" title="Sebastián Cordero">
         Sebastián Cordero
        </a>
        (b. 1972, Quito)
       </li>
       <li>
        Painter
        <a href="/wiki/Oswaldo_Guayasam%C3%ADn" title="Oswaldo Guayasamín">
         Oswaldo Guayasamín
        </a>
        (b. 1919, Quito – d. 1999, Baltimore U.S.)
       </li>
       <li>
        Professional Footballer
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_Benitez" title="Christian Benitez">
         Christian Benitez
        </a>
        (b. May 1, 1986, Quito – d. July 29, 2013, Doha, Qatar)
       </li>
       <li>
        Catholic Saint
        <a href="/wiki/Mariana_de_Jes%C3%BAs_de_Paredes" title="Mariana de Jesús de Paredes">
         Mariana de Jesús de Paredes
        </a>
        (b.1618, Quito – d. 1645, Quito)
       </li>
       <li>
        Scientist
        <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Espejo" title="Eugenio Espejo">
         Eugenio Espejo
        </a>
        (b. February 21, 1747 – d. December, 1795)
       </li>
      </ul>
